mysql> SELECT " so, what happend above is when RIGHT JOIN used it brings every selcted item (order_date in this case) from the table on the right (ie orders) and matchesthe corresponding customer_id's to id's in the left table (ie cutomers) to filter the selected items from that table (ie. last_name's). When LEFT JOIN used something interesting happened- all selected items (last_names) from the table on the left (customers) were returned. From the right table all the order_dates returned. Because NOT all customers made orders, some last_names correspond to NULL order_date. Same concept in PANDAS.' AS NOTE;   
    "> "AS NOTE;
+----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------+
| NOTE                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
+----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------+
|  so, what happend above is when RIGHT JOIN used it brings every selcted item (order_date in this case) from the table on the right (ie orders) and matchesthe corresponding customer_id's to id's in the left table (ie cutomers) to filter the selected items from that table (ie. last_name's). When LEFT JOIN used something interesting happened- all selected items (last_names) from the table on the left (customers) were returned. From the right table all the order_dates returned. Because NOT all customers made orders, some last_names correspond to NULL order_date. Same concept in PANDAS.' AS NOTE;   
 |

    ->          WHEN orders.amount IS NOT NULL THEN CONCAT_WS(' ', 'Dear', first_name, last_name, ', thank you for your last order on', order_date,'.')
    ->          ELSE CONCAT_WS(' ', 'Dear', first_name, last_name, ', you have yet to make an order. What the hell are you waiting for?') 
    ->      END AS 'customer appreciation day email draft'

    ->           ON customers.id = orders.customer_id;

mysql> -- in the above 'ON reviews.reviewer_id = series.id' results in a meaningless table. Rather use 'ON reviews.series_id = series.id' so that the resut is a filtering of series that have been reviewed.
mysql> 
mysql> 
mysql>

mysql> -- For this we need reviews and series  tables
mysql> SELECT series.genre, AVG(reviews.rating) as avg_rating FROM series
    -> JOIN reviews
    ->     ON series.id = reviews.series_id
    -> GROUP BY 1;
+-----------+------------+
| genre     | avg_rating |
+-----------+------------+
| Animation |    7.86000 |
| Comedy    |    8.16250 |
| Drama     |    8.04375 |
+-----------+------------+
3 rows in set (0.00 sec)

mysql> -- glad to see Commedy- the only genre I would spend time watching- is the top rated genre.
mysql> -- these are real data altough I suspect slightly outdated.
mysql> 
mysql> 
mysql> SELECT series.genre, ROUND(AVG(reviews.rating), 2) as avg_rating FROM series
    -> JOIN reviews
    ->     ON series.id = reviews.series_id
    -> GROUP BY 1;
+-----------+------------+
| genre     | avg_rating |
+-----------+------------+
| Animation |       7.86 |
| Comedy    |       8.16 |
| Drama     |       8.04 |
+-----------+------------+
3 rows in set (0.03 sec)

mysql> -- ROUND seems a universal function across languages;
mysql>
